<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A switched resonator concept, which can be used to reduce the size of multiple-band RF systems and which allows better tradeoff between phase noise and power consumption, is demonstrated using a dual-band voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO) in a 0.18-/spl mu/m CMOS process. To maximize Q of the switched resonator when the switch is on, the mutual inductance between the inductors should be kept low and the switch transistor size should be optimized. The Q factor of switched resonators is /spl sim/30% lower than that of a standalone inductor. The dual-band VCO operates near 900 MHz and 1.8 GHz with phase noise of -125 and -123dBc/Hz at a 600-kHz offset and 16-mW power consumption. Compared to a single-band 1.8-GHz VCO, the dual-band VCO has almost the same phase noise and power consumption, while occupying /spl sim/37% smaller area.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>THE proliferation of wireless applications is rapidly increasing the demand for low-cost communication terminals, which can support multiple standards and frequency bands. In response to this, multiband terminals using multiple RF transceivers have been reported
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig>Schematic of a dual-band VCO.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. This, however, increases die area or chip count in a radio, which, in turn, increases cost and complexity of radios. A way to mitigate this is the use of a tunable/programmable transceiver consisting of a tunable low-noise amplifier <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, buffers and mixers, and a voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO) with a wide tuning range. To realize the tunable RF blocks, the variable inductor concept has been previously reported <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>– <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> and utilized first in a VCO <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The VCO partially relies on the changes in series resistance of an inductor to attain continuous variations of effective inductance. This resistance, however, significantly degrades <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the resonator and phase noise of the VCO. To reduce the degradation of phase noise, a switched resonator concept (dotted rectangle in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>) is proposed and demonstrated in a dual-band VCO, and a VCO with a tuning range greater than 50% and excellent phase-noise performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. In fact, the VCO in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> achieves the lowest phase noise among CMOS VCOs operating near 2.4 and 5.2 GHz. In this paper, the measured and simulated characteristics of switched resonators including the quality factor are reported. Analytical expressions, which explain the behaviors of switched resonators, as well as the design considerations and approaches to improve their properties are presented. Lastly, this paper suggests that a dual-band VCO using switched resonators can have the same phase noise and power consumption while occupying a smaller area than that for two VCOs needed to cover the two bands.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Need for a Switched Resonator</h2></div><p>A possible way to achieve a wide tuning range is to use a switched capacitor bank in a resonator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a>. To qualitatively discuss the need for a switched resonator over a switched capacitor bank, consider the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>–<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> VCO shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. Since the quality factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the on-chip spiral inductor is significantly lower than that of the capacitances in the resonator, especially at frequencies between 1–2 GHz, the equivalent total parallel resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ P}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be approximated by the equivalent parallel resistance of the inductor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ PL}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ PL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For an inductor with series resistance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ SL}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ SL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and inductance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ PL}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ PL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\omega{L})^{2}/{R}_{ SL}</span><script type="math/tex">(\omega{L})^{2}/{R}_{ SL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ SL}\cdot {Q}_{\rm ind}^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ SL}\cdot {Q}_{\rm ind}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega</span><script type="math/tex">\omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the desired oscillation frequency. To sustain oscillation, the loop gain <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{G}_{ M} \cdot {(\omega {L})^{2} \over {R}_{ SL}} ={G}_{ M}\cdot{R}_{ SL}\cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}^{2} = 1 \eqno\hbox{(1)}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{G}_{ M} \cdot {(\omega {L})^{2} \over {R}_{ SL}} ={G}_{ M}\cdot{R}_{ SL}\cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}^{2} = 1 \eqno\hbox{(1)}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{G}_{ M} \cdot {(\omega {L})^{2} \over {R}_{ SL}} ={G}_{ M}\cdot{R}_{ SL}\cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}^{2} = 1 \eqno\hbox{(1)}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{G}_{ M}</span><script type="math/tex">{G}_{ M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the effective transconductance of the VCO core transistors.</p><p>With the assumption that, for a given process technology, when inductance changes, its series resistance also changes with approximately the same ratio, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximately constant, if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is larger, then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{G}_{ M}</span><script type="math/tex">{G}_{ M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be smaller or power consumption of the VCO can be reduced since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{G}_{ M}\cdot(\omega{L})^{2}/{R}_{ SL}=1</span><script type="math/tex">{G}_{ M}\cdot(\omega{L})^{2}/{R}_{ SL}=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Due to this, if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega</span><script type="math/tex">\omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is reduced by increasing only the capacitance, then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{G}_{ M}</span><script type="math/tex">{G}_{ M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> must be increased as (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">1/\omega^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">1/\omega^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). This results in significantly higher power consumption and core transistor size than would be needed if both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> were to be increased.</p><p>At the same time, increasing only <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> arbitrarily high will increase the series resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ SL}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ SL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. When the core voltage swing is near the maximum, which is how VCOs are typically designed to operate, this will limit the phase-noise performance. This is also undesirable and points to the need for a switched resonator in which both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be tuned. The phase-noise limitation imposed by arbitrarily increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be explained using the Leeson–Cutler phase-noise equation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a> as follows:<disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{L}(\Delta \omega) \cong &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF}} \over {{P}_{ S}}} \cdot \left [1 + {\left({{\omega _{0}}\over { 2{Q}_{{\rm tank}}{\Delta \omega}}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr = &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF} \omega_{0}{LQ}_{\rm ind}}\over {{V}^{2}_{\rm rms}}} \left[1+{\left({{\omega_{0}}\over{2{Q}_{{\rm ind}} \Delta \omega}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr&amp;&amp;\hbox{(2)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eqalignno{{L}(\Delta \omega) \cong &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF}} \over {{P}_{ S}}} \cdot \left [1 + {\left({{\omega _{0}}\over { 2{Q}_{{\rm tank}}{\Delta \omega}}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr = &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF} \omega_{0}{LQ}_{\rm ind}}\over {{V}^{2}_{\rm rms}}} \left[1+{\left({{\omega_{0}}\over{2{Q}_{{\rm ind}} \Delta \omega}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr&amp;&amp;\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{L}(\Delta \omega) \cong &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF}} \over {{P}_{ S}}} \cdot \left [1 + {\left({{\omega _{0}}\over { 2{Q}_{{\rm tank}}{\Delta \omega}}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr = &amp;\, 10 \cdot \log \left\{{{2{kTF} \omega_{0}{LQ}_{\rm ind}}\over {{V}^{2}_{\rm rms}}} \left[1+{\left({{\omega_{0}}\over{2{Q}_{{\rm ind}} \Delta \omega}}\right)^{2}}\right]\right\} \cr&amp;&amp;\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{k}</span><script type="math/tex">{k}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the Boltzmann's constant, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{T}</span><script type="math/tex">{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the absolute temperature, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{F}</span><script type="math/tex">{F}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the noise factor of core transistors/amplifiers, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{P}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{P}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the average power dissipated in the tank, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega _{0}</span><script type="math/tex">\omega _{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the oscillation frequency, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm tank}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm tank}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the quality factor of the total tank, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta \omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the offset from the carrier. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{P}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{P}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm rms}^2/{R}_{ P}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm rms}^2/{R}_{ P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm rms}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm rms}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the root mean square voltage across the tank. As mentioned, since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\tank}\cong{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\tank}\cong{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the total parallel resistance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ P}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the tank is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim{R}_{ SL}\cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}^{2}=\omega_{0}{L} \cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim{R}_{ SL}\cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}^{2}=\omega_{0}{L} \cdot{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, when the voltage swing is near the maximum, for given <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, phase noise is only determined by the noise factor and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Due to this, to reduce phase noise, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be lowered.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig>(a) and (b) Two-use configurations of a switched resonator. (c) An equivalent circuit of a switched resonator in (a). (d) The equivalent circuit when port 2 is ac grounded and the switch is on. (e) The equivalent circuit when the switch is off.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>These mean if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is chosen for the higher frequency band and the same <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used for the lower frequency band using a large switched capacitor bank, the power consumption at the lower frequency band may be higher than needed. Since the core transistor size should be made larger to support the larger power consumption, this will also reduce the VCO tuning range especially at the higher band. On the other hand, if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is chosen for the lower frequency band, then phase-noise performance at the higher frequency band will be compromised. Due to these, an element in which both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be simultaneously tuned provides a greater flexibility to trade off phase noise, power consumption, and tuning range due to greater flexibility for choosing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and enables implementation of a VCO with given phase noise over a large frequency range at lower power consumption. Lastly, for VCOs implemented in deep submicrometer CMOS processes, another contributor to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ P}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of a tank is the output resistance of the transistors. As will be discussed, this can reduce the impact of lower <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of switched resonators.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Switched Resonator Concept</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a> shows switched resonators including mutual inductance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). The inductance seen between ports 1 and 2 are changed by turning the switch transistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{\rm sw}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{\rm sw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on and off. The equivalent circuit of the switched resonator is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a>. In the case that port 2 is grounded and that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have no mutual effect (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}=0</span><script type="math/tex">{M}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), the resonator is simplified into the circuit in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(d)</a> when the switch is on, and into the circuit in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(e)</a> when off. When the switch is off, the inductance of switched resonator is largely determined by the two inductors while the capacitance is determined by the parasitic capacitances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ pL} 1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ pL} 1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ pL} 2}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ pL} 2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the inductors and the capacitances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{ db}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{ db}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{\rm gd}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{\rm gd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) at the drain of the switch transistor.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig>Photomicrographs of switched resonators with parallel and offset topologies. (a) An offset structure with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{W}/{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{W}/{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm NMOS} = 2 {\hbox { mm}}/0.18\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">{\rm NMOS} = 2 {\hbox { mm}}/0.18\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) A parallel structure with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{W}/{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{W}/{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm NMOS} = 2 {\hbox { mm}}/0.18\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">{\rm NMOS} = 2 {\hbox { mm}}/0.18\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The current directions of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">i_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">i_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">i_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">i_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are shown on the inductors.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> The extracted inductance using measurements and the simple inductor model is lower due to the effects of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{\rm gd}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{\rm gd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in series with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{ db}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{ db}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the switch transistor (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>. When the switch is on, the channel resistance is close to zero. The inductance and capacitance of the switched resonator are switched by shorting out <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the capacitances associated with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the switch transistor. The inductance is approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the capacitance is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p} 1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p} 1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, thus, leading to simultaneous decreases of inductance and capacitance.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Design and Extracted Parameters of the Switched Resonators</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the test structures used to develop better understanding of the characteristics and limitations of switched resonators. The structures were fabricated in a 0.18-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a>] have 3.25 turns with a metal linewidth of 19 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and 4.25 turns with a metal width of 10 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. The inductors are formed by shunting metal 3–5 layers. The total metal thickness is 4 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The switch transistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{\rm sw}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{\rm sw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is 0.18-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> long. This small channel length is required to minimize the channel resistance and to minimize the quality-factor reduction when the switch is on. Due to uses of short gate fingers, the gate resistance is sufficiently low and its impact is negligible. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are separated and offset to reduce the impact of mutual inductance between the inductors. The structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> has an nMOS switch transistor (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{\rm sw}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{\rm sw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) with a width of 2 mm. Though not shown, another structure similar to that in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> with a transistor width of 1 mm also has been fabricated. The simulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{\rm on}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{\rm on}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm inductor}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm inductor}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 2.7 V (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{\rm sw} = 1.8~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{\rm sw} = 1.8~{\hbox{V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), which can be generated using a voltage doubler <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_4">[17]</a> are 0.4 and 0.8 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> compared to 2.1 and 2.9 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> low-frequency series resistances of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Although low, this finite <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{\rm on}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{\rm on}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE I </b>Switched Resonator in Fig. 3(a)<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig>(a) Lumped-element model for a planar spiral inductor. (b) Measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (c) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (d) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and (e) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency plots for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L} _{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L} _{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L} _{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L} _{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>For the structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are located in parallel. This increases the mutual inductance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) between the structures to 0.26 nH. This, however, is still significantly smaller than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In addition to these, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are separately fabricated to study the impact of using the inductors in switched resonator structures. The extracted inductances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from measurements using an HP8510C two-port network analyzer are 4.7 and 6.1 nH, the series resistances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) are 1.7 and 3.1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the parasitic capacitances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) are 500 and 360 fF, respectively (<a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>). <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are measured at 45 MHz. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p} 1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p} 1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is measured at 300 MHz. The equivalent-circuit model and plots for the model parameters and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_4">[18]</a> versus frequency are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ s}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases more rapidly with frequency than that expected from the skin and proximity effects and, at frequencies above 3 GHz, it decreases. These are due to modeling the inductor using a simple lumped model [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a>] rather than using a distributed model <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_4">[16]</a>.<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig>Plots of: (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (c) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and (d) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency when the switch is on. (e) The lumped-element model for a switched resonator.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig>Plots of measured and simulated: (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, (c) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and (d) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency when the switch is off.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a> show the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(e)</a>] for the switched resonator when the switch is on and off, respectively. The dc voltage of 0.9 V is applied to ports 1 and 2. The threshold voltage of the switching transistor is increased due to the body effect, which slightly increases the on resistance.<p></p><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have stronger frequency dependence than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and can even become negative. The stronger frequency dependence of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and negative <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are due to the fact that, in the presence of additional parasitic capacitances (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{\rm gd}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{\rm gd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (630 fF) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{ db}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{ db}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (790 fF), the effects of modeling a distributed structure using a simple lumped section become stronger <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_4">[16]</a>. The structure resonates at the frequencies near <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff} =0</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff} =0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The self-resonant frequencies of structures are significantly reduced compared to that for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. However, the structures are still useful at frequencies below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 2.5 GHz}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 2.5 GHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when the switch is on and below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 1.5 GHz}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 1.5 GHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when the switch is off.</p><p>When the switch is on, assuming the channel resistance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math
