eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The models for individual inductors and transistor are used for the simulations. The measured and simulated results are in qualitative agreement, especially within the intended operating frequency range between 1–2 GHz. Except for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, when the switch is on, the simulation results below 2 GHz are within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim\ 30\%</span><script type="math/tex">\sim\ 30\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the measured results.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> shows <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(e)</a>] versus the gate-to-source voltage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the switch for the structures shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. As the transistor in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> is switched from off to on, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decrease, but <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">(d)</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. This <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increase is due to the channel resistance and resistances in series with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{ db}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{ db}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{\rm gd}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{\rm gd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Due to the frequency dependences, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are specified at the lowest measurement frequency, and to avoid measurement errors, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are extracted at higher frequency, but significantly lower than the self-resonant frequency.</p><p>Comparing the characteristics of the structures in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a>, when the switch is on, the mutual inductance effect slightly reduces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>, while increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the structure. These slightly reduce <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a>]. When the switch is off, the mutual effect makes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> become slightly greater [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a>] than the sum of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, but negligibly affects <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximately the sum of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s}2}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s}2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. The structures in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a> have comparable <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a>]. The effects of mutual inductance is small because <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is only <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim { {\rm 0.26 nH}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim { {\rm 0.26 nH}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This indicates that offsetting inductors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not critical.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig>Plots of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency: (a) when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs} = -0.9~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs} = -0.9~{\hbox{V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and (b) when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs} = 3.6~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs} = 3.6~{\hbox{V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (c) A plot of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and (d) a plot of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 0.9 and 1.8 GHz when the switch is on and off.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>Referring to the structures in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">(c)</a>, when the width of the switching transistor is larger, the on-resistance is smaller. However, because the parasitic capacitances are bigger, the current and loss through the substrate becomes larger. Therefore, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_4">[18]</a> is lowered when the transistor width is too large [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a>]. On the other hand, if the width is too small, then the on resistance can be too high and this also lowers <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This means there is an optimal size for the switching transistor to maximize <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> similar to the insertion-loss dependence on transistor width in MOS T/R switches <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_4">[19]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(c)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">(d)</a> shows the maximum quality factor (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_4">[18]</a> over the measurement frequency range and quality factor (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) versus the gate-to-source voltage plot of the switch at 900 and 1800 MHz. Among the structures, the switched resonator with a 1-mm-wide transistor has the highest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the intended operating frequencies of 0.9 and 1.8 GHz.<p></p><p>When the switch is on and off, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s are 6.5 and 6.9, respectively, and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s are 5.2 and 6.9, respectively for the structure with offset and 2-mm width (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>). The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s are 6.5 and 7.4 and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>'s are 5.7 and 7.3 for the structure with offset and 1-mm width when the switch is on and off. Increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> beyond 1.8 V has an almost negligible effect on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm bw}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm bw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. When the switch is on, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the structure with offset and 1-mm width is reduced by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim 34\%</span><script type="math/tex">\sim 34\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> compared to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{{\rm bw},\max }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by itself. When the switch is on, compared to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are increased by 0.5 nH and 0.9 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>,
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig>Measured tuning ranges of a dual-band VCO and that for a single-band VCO.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> respectively, due to the nonnegligible on resistance [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a>]. This increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{ s},{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{{\rm sub}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(d)</a>] reduce <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The transitions of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a> are sharp primarily due to the low on resistance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{\rm on}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{\rm on}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{\rm sw}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{\rm sw}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Since the switch transistor is wide, its contribution to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is significant. When the mutual inductance is large, the slope of transition of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will be more gradual. This combination of inductance and capacitance changes results in a large frequency tuning range, and can provide a better tradeoff between power consumption and phase noise in VCOs. The measured results for the switched resonator in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. Lastly, the extracted parameters are frequency dependent due to the simple model that was used to represent the switched resonators. Clearly, more research is needed to develop a better model.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Design of the Dual-Band VCO</h2></div><p>To evaluate the usefulness of switched resonators, a dual-band VCO shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> was fabricated. In the dual-band VCO, on top of the conventional pMOS VCO core composed of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M} _{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{M} _{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and buffers composed of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{6}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{6}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{7}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_5">[20]</a>, there are transistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and inductors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. By controlling the gate voltage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm inductor}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm inductor}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the inductance of the tanks can be controlled. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L} _{3}</span><script type="math/tex">{L} _{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are 4.7 nH and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are 6.1 nH. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}+{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}+{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is set to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{2}} \times</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{2}} \times</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are off, the inductance of tanks is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim { {\rm 7.9 nH}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim { {\rm 7.9 nH}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 2.9 pF}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 2.9 pF}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the VCO operates in the 0.9-GHz band [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(e)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">(f)</a>]. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are on, the inductance is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim { {\rm 3.2 nH}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim { {\rm 3.2 nH}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 1.5 pF}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 1.5 pF}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is around half of that for the 0.9-GHz operation, and the VCO operates in the 1.8-GHz band. The simultaneous reduction of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{\rm eff}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{\rm eff}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</span><script type="math/tex">{C}_{{ p}1,{\rm eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases the resonant frequency. Fine tuning of the VCO is accomplished using p<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{+}</span><script type="math/tex">{+}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-n<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"> {-}</span><script type="math/tex"> {-}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> well varactor diodes. This lowers VCO gains in each band, which should lower phase noise <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_5">[9]</a> and provide added immunity from the phase-locked loop (PLL) instability and noise pick-up problems.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE II </b>VCO Characteristics at <span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{ DD}=1.8~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{ DD}=1.8~{\hbox{V}}</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig>Measured quality factors of a switched resonator and the phase noise at 600-kHz offset from carriers around 0.9 and 1.8 GHz versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in a dual-band VCO when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{ sb} = 0.6~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{ sb} = 0.6~{\hbox{V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{I}_{\rm bias} = 8.8~{\hbox {mA}}</span><script type="math/tex">{I}_{\rm bias} = 8.8~{\hbox {mA}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{ sb} = 0.9~{\hbox{V}}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{ sb} = 0.9~{\hbox{V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 3.3 mA.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Experimental Results of the Dual-Band VCO</h2></div><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, the tuning range for the 0.8-GHz band is between 0.753–0.867 GHz over the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm control}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm control}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> range between 0.5–3.6 V, which corresponds to a 13% tuning range. However, the phase noise is flat and low only for frequencies between 0.823–0.867 GHz, which corresponds to a 5% tuning range. The tuning range for the 1.8-GHz band is 1.381–1.814 GHz over the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm control}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm control}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> range between 0.4–3.6 V, which corresponds to a 24% tuning range. However, once again, phase noise is flat and low only for frequencies between 1.640–1.814 GHz, which corresponds to a 9% tuning range. These reductions in the usable tuning range are due to the forward-biasing of p-n varactors, and this problem can be alleviated by using a MOS varactor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_6">[21]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_6">[22]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_6">[23]</a>. In fact, a switched resonator has been used in conjunction with MOS varactors to realize VCOs with a wide tuning range while achieving comparable phase-noise performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_6">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_6">[10]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> also shows the simulated tuning ranges, which are in reasonable agreement with the measurements.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE III </b>Performance of VCO's Using Either a Variable Inductor or a Switched Resonator<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/33279/1573798/1573798-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig>Photomicrographs of a dual- and single-band VCO.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1573798/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>The measured phase noise for the low band is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox{125 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</span><script type="math/tex">-{\hbox{125 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a 600-kHz offset from a 0.865-GHz carrier and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox{123 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</span><script type="math/tex">-{\hbox{123 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a 600-kHz offset from a 1.812-GHz carrier for the high band. In addition, a 1.8-GHz VCO without a switched resonator has been fabricated for performance comparison. The measured results are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>. The phase noise of this single-band VCO is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox{123 dBc}}/{\hbox {Hz}}</span><script type="math/tex">-{\hbox{123 dBc}}/{\hbox {Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a 600-kHz offset from a 1.894-GHz carrier, which is almost the same as the phase noise of the dual-band VCO at the high band. The power consumption of both the single and dual-band VCOs with a 1.8-V supply is 16 mW. The similar phase noise and power consumption for the dual- and single-band VCOs near 1.8 GHz are surprising, given the lower <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the switched resonator of the dual-band VCO. A plausible explanation for this is that the parallel resistance of the resonator is not solely determined by the equivalent parallel resistance of inductor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{ P}</span><script type="math/tex">{R}_{ P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Instead, it could be determined or significantly affected by the output resistance of the amplifiers in the VCO core. Especially for deep submicrometer transistors with channel lengths of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 0.18}}~\mu{{\rm m}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 0.18}}~\mu{{\rm m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and below, the effects of output resistances will not be negligible. During the portions of an oscillation cycle when the core amplifier is on, the output resistances vary from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim 1000</span><script type="math/tex">\sim 1000</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 250}}~\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 250}}~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> compared to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 300-}}\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 300-}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> parallel resistance of the tank (excluding the transistor output resistance).<p></p><p>The phase noise at a 600-kHz offset from around a 900-MHz and 1.8-GHz carrier and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}_{\rm ind}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}_{\rm ind}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus the gate-to-source voltage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{\rm gs}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{\rm gs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the switching transistor are measured and shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>. The maximum output swing and minimum phase noise in the VCO occur when the measured dc voltage at the source of the tail transistor (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{V}_{ sb}</span><script type="math/tex">{V}_{ sb}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{3}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{\rm 0.6 V}}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{\rm 0.6 V}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{I}_{\rm bias}</span><script type="math/tex">{I}_{\rm bias}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 8.8 mA. Phase noise is high around the threshold voltage due to the low <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(d)</a>]. In fact, the oscillation is lost near the threshold voltage once the phase noise becomes higher than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox{112 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</span><script type="math/tex">-{\hbox{112 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the 600-kHz offset.</p><p>The figure-of-merit (FOM) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_6">[24]</a> in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> is the widely used FOM for the VCO, which is defined as <disp-formula id="deqn8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm FOM}={L}\left\{{f}_{\rm offset}\right\} - 20 \log{\left({{{f}_{ c}} \over{{f}_{\rm offset}}}\right)} + 10 \log{\left({{{P}_{\rm DC}} \over {1~{\hbox {mW}}^{\cdot}}}\right)}.\eqno\hbox{(8)}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{\rm FOM}={L}\left\{{f}_{\rm offset}\right\} - 20 \log{\left({{{f}_{ c}} \over{{f}_{\rm offset}}}\right)} + 10 \log{\left({{{P}_{\rm DC}} \over {1~{\hbox {mW}}^{\cdot}}}\right)}.\eqno\hbox{(8)}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm FOM}={L}\left\{{f}_{\rm offset}\right\} - 20 \log{\left({{{f}_{ c}} \over{{f}_{\rm offset}}}\right)} + 10 \log{\left({{{P}_{\rm DC}} \over {1~{\hbox {mW}}^{\cdot}}}\right)}.\eqno\hbox{(8)}</span></span></disp-formula><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}\{{f}_{\rm offset}\}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}\{{f}_{\rm offset}\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the measured phase noise at offset frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{f}_{\rm offset}</span><script type="math/tex">{f}_{\rm offset}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the carrier frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{f}_{ c}</span><script type="math/tex">{f}_{ c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{P}_{\rm DC}</span><script type="math/tex">{P}_{\rm DC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the VCO power consumption in milliwatts. The FOMs of VCOs presented in this paper range between −176 and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-{\hbox{182 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</span><script type="math/tex">-{\hbox{182 dBc}}/{\hbox{Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. These are not the best, but are competitive. This indicates that the VCOs are reasonable test vehicles for studying the impact of switch resonators on the VCO performance.</p><p>The chip micrograph for the dual-band VCO is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are offset. The area increase due to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is small. The die sizes of the dual- and the single-band VCO are 1.3×0.7 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 0.86×0.68 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> including the output buffers, respectively. The dual-band VCO excluding the output buffers and pads is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim { {\rm 0.598 mm}}^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim { {\rm 0.598 mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and is increased by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim {{41}}\%</span><script type="math/tex">\sim {{41}}\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> compared to that of the single-band 1.8-GHz VCO, which is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim { {\rm 0.351 mm}}^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">\sim { {\rm 0.351 mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This increase is due to the areas of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{L}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{L}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{4}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{5}</span><script type="math/tex">{M}_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>. Compared to two single-band VCO core areas, this dual-band VCO should occupy <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim 37\%</span><script type="math/tex">\sim 37\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> smaller area.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>The dependences of characteristics for switched resonators, which provide greater flexibility to trade off phase noise, tuning range, and power consumption of VCOs on frequency and the gate-to-source voltage of switch transistors has been presented. The model parameters of switched resonators have stronger frequency dependence than those for inductors. Compared to the resonators that can be constructed using on-chip inductors, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of switched resonators is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim 30\%</span><script type="math/tex">\sim 30\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> lower. The dependences of model parameters for switched resonators on the parameters of their subcomponents are explained. The effects of mutual inductance between the switched inductors have been investigated and shown to be insignificant. There are optimal sizes for the transistors in switched resonators to maximize <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Q}</span><script type="math/tex">{Q}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when the transistors are on. By comparing a dual-band VCO using switched resonators operating near 0.9 and 1.8 GHz, and a single-band 1.8-GHz VCO, it has been shown that the dual-band VCO with switched resonators can have the same phase noise and power consumption while occupying a smaller area than that for two VCOs needed to cover the two bands.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors are grateful to Dr. J. Zheng, P. N. Sherman, B. Krieger, and P. Kempf, all with Jazz Semiconductor, Newport Beach, CA, for their help.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
